The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominican_friar" title="Dominican friar">Dominican friar</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_de_Las_Casas" title="Bartolomé de Las Casas">Bartolomé de Las Casas</a> wrote his <i><a href="/wiki/A_Short_Account_of_the_Destruction_of_the_Indies" title="A Short Account of the Destruction of the Indies">A Short Account of the Destruction of the Indies</a></i> which raises strong accusations of brutality and heinous violence towards the Indians; accusations against both the conquistadors in general and Cortés in particular.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WDL_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-WDL-43">[43]</a></sup> The accounts of the conquest given in the <a href="/wiki/Florentine_Codex" title="Florentine Codex">Florentine Codex</a> by the Franciscan <a href="/wiki/Bernardino_de_Sahag%C3%BAn" title="Bernardino de Sahagún">Bernardino de Sahagún</a> and his native informants are also less than flattering towards Cortés. The scarcity of these sources has led to a sharp division in the description of Cortés's personality and a tendency to describe him as either a vicious and ruthless person or a noble and honorable cavalier.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Representations_in_Mexico">Representations in Mexico</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_de_Moctezuma_y_Hernan_Cort%C3%A9s.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Monumento_de_Moctezuma_y_Hernan_Cort%C3%A9s.jpg/230px-Monumento_de_Moctezuma_y_Hernan_Cort%C3%A9s.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Monumento_de_Moctezuma_y_Hernan_Cort%C3%A9s.jpg/345px-Monumento_de_Moctezuma_y_Hernan_Cort%C3%A9s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Monumento_de_Moctezuma_y_Hernan_Cort%C3%A9s.jpg/460px-Monumento_de_Moctezuma_y_Hernan_Cort%C3%A9s.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_de_Moctezuma_y_Hernan_Cort%C3%A9s.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Monument in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a> commemorating the encounter of Cortés and Moctezuma at the Hospital de Jesús Nazareno.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In México there are few representations of Cortés. However, many landmarks still bear his name, from the castle <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palace_of_Cortes,_Cuernavaca" title="Palace of Cortes, Cuernavaca">Palacio de Cortés</a> in the city of <a href="/wiki/Cuernavaca" title="Cuernavaca">Cuernavaca</a> to some street names throughout the republic.</p>
<p>The only authentic monuments are in Mexico City at the pass between the volcanoes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iztacc%C3%ADhuatl" title="Iztaccíhuatl">Iztaccíhuatl</a> and <a href="/wiki/Popocat%C3%A9petl" title="Popocatépetl">Popocatépetl</a> where Cortés took his soldiers on their march to Mexico City. It is known as the <a href="/wiki/Paso_de_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Paso de Cortés">Paso de Cortés</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Mural" title="Mural">muralist</a> <a href="/wiki/Diego_Rivera" title="Diego Rivera">Diego Rivera</a> painted several representation of him but the most famous, depicts him as a powerful and ominous figure along with Malinche in a mural in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Palace_of_Mexico" title="National Palace of Mexico">National Palace</a> in Mexico City.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_al_Mestizaje.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Monumento_al_Mestizaje.jpg/230px-Monumento_al_Mestizaje.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Monumento_al_Mestizaje.jpg/345px-Monumento_al_Mestizaje.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Monumento_al_Mestizaje.jpg/460px-Monumento_al_Mestizaje.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Monumento_al_Mestizaje.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Monument in Mexico City known as "Monumento al Mestizaje".</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1981, President <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lopez_Portillo" title="Lopez Portillo">Lopez Portillo</a> tried to bring Cortés to public recognition. First, he made public a copy of the bust of Cortés made by <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Tols%C3%A1" title="Manuel Tolsá">Manuel Tolsá</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Hospital_de_Jes%C3%BAs_Nazareno" title="Hospital de Jesús Nazareno">Hospital de Jesús Nazareno</a> with an official ceremony, but soon a nationalist group tried to destroy it, so it had to be taken out of the public.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-letraslibres1_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-letraslibres1-44">[44]</a></sup> Today the copy of bust is in the "Hospital de Jesús Nazareno" <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> while the original is in Naples, Italy, in the <a href="/wiki/Villa_Pignatelli" title="Villa Pignatelli">Villa Pignatelli</a>.</p>
<p>Later, another monument, known as "Monumento al Mestizaje" by Julián Martínez y M. Maldonado (1982) was commissioned by Mexican president José López Portillo to be put in the "Zócalo" (Main square) of Coyoacan, near the place of his country house, but it had to be removed to a little known park, the Jardín Xicoténcatl, Barrio de San Diego Churubusco, to quell protests. The statue depicts Cortés, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malinche" title="Malinche">Malinche</a> and their son Martín.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>There is another statue by Sebastián Aparicio, in Cuernavaca, was in a hotel "El casino de la selva". Cortés is barely recognizable, so it sparked little interest. The hotel was closed to make a commercial center, and the statue was put out of public display by Costco the builder of the commercial center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-letraslibres1_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-letraslibres1-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_depictions">Cultural depictions</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lorenzo_Ferrero_-_Scene_from_the_opera_La_Conquista.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="850" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Lorenzo_Ferrero_-_Scene_from_the_opera_La_Conquista.jpg/240px-Lorenzo_Ferrero_-_Scene_from_the_opera_La_Conquista.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Lorenzo_Ferrero_-_Scene_from_the_opera_La_Conquista.jpg/360px-Lorenzo_Ferrero_-_Scene_from_the_opera_La_Conquista.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Lorenzo_Ferrero_-_Scene_from_the_opera_La_Conquista.jpg/480px-Lorenzo_Ferrero_-_Scene_from_the_opera_La_Conquista.jpg 2x" width="240"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lorenzo_Ferrero_-_Scene_from_the_opera_La_Conquista.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Scene from the opera <i><a href="/wiki/La_Conquista_(opera)" title="La Conquista (opera)">La Conquista</a></i>, 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hernán Cortés is a character in the opera <i><a href="/wiki/La_Conquista_(opera)" title="La Conquista (opera)">La Conquista</a></i> (2005) by Italian composer <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Ferrero" title="Lorenzo Ferrero">Lorenzo Ferrero</a>, which depicts the major episodes of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Aztec_Empire" title="Spanish conquest of the Aztec Empire">Spanish conquest of the Aztec Empire</a> in 1521.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Writings:_the_Cartas_de_Relaci.C3.B3n">Writings: the <i>Cartas de Relación</i></span></h3>
<p>Cortés' personal account of the conquest of Mexico is narrated in his five letters addressed to Charles V. These five letters, the <i>cartas de relación</i>, are Cortés' only surviving writings. See "Letters and Dispatches of Cortés", translated by George Folsom (New York, 1843); Prescott's "Conquest of Mexico" (Boston, 1843); and Sir Arthur Helps's "Life of Hernando Cortes" (London, 1871).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-virtualology1_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-virtualology1-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>His first letter is lost, and the one from the municipality of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veracruz,_Veracruz" title="Veracruz, Veracruz">Veracruz</a> has to take its place. It was published for the first time in volume IV of "Documentos para la Historia de España", and subsequently reprinted. The first <i>carta de relación</i> is available online at the University of Wisconsin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Segunda Carta de Relacion</i>, bearing the date of October 30, 1520, appeared in print at <a href="/wiki/Seville" title="Seville">Seville</a> in 1522. The <a href="/wiki/Third_letter_of_Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s_to_the_Emperor_Charles_V" title="Third letter of Hernán Cortés to the Emperor Charles V">third letter</a>, dated May 15, 1522, appeared at Seville in 1523. The fourth, October 20, 1524, was printed at <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Spain" title="Toledo, Spain">Toledo</a> in 1525. The fifth, on the Honduras expedition, is contained in volume IV of the <i>Documentos para la Historia de España</i>. The important letter mentioned in the text has been published under the heading of <i>Carta inédita de Cortés</i> by Ycazbalceta. A great number of minor documents, either by Cortés or others, for or against him, are dispersed through the voluminous collection above cited and through the <i>Colección de Documentos de Indias</i>, as well as in the <i>Documentos para la Historia de México</i> of Ycazbalceta. There are a number of reprints and translations of Cortés's writings into various languages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Children">Children</span></h2>
<p>Natural children of Don Hernán Cortés</p>
<ul>
<li><i>doña</i> Catalina Pizarro, born between 1514 and 1515 in <a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Cuba" title="Santiago de Cuba">Santiago de Cuba</a> or maybe later in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nueva_Espa%C3%B1a" title="Nueva España">Nueva España</a>, daughter of a Cuban woman, Leonor Pizarro. Doña Catalina married Juan de Salcedo, a conqueror and encomendero, with whom she had a son, Pedro.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>don</i> <a href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADn_Cort%C3%A9s_(son_of_do%C3%B1a_Marina)" title="Martín Cortés (son of doña Marina)">Martín Cortés</a>, born in <a href="/wiki/Coyoac%C3%A1n" title="Coyoacán">Coyoacán</a> in 1522, son of <i>doña</i> Marina (La Malinche), called the <i>First Mestizo</i>; about him was written <i>The New World of Martín Cortés</i>; married <i>doña</i> Bernaldina de Porras and had two children:
<ul>
<li><i>doña</i> Ana Cortés</li>
<li><i>don</i> Fernando Cortés, Principal <a href="/wiki/Judge" title="Judge">Judge</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Veracruz,_Veracruz" title="Veracruz, Veracruz">Veracruz</a>. Descendants of this line are alive today in Mexico.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><i>don</i> Luis Cortés, born in 1525, son of <i>doña</i> Antonia or Elvira Hermosillo, a native of Trujillo (Cáceres)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>doña</i> <a href="/wiki/Leonor_Cort%C3%A9s_Moctezuma" title="Leonor Cortés Moctezuma">Leonor Cortés Moctezuma</a>, born in 1527 or 1528 in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ciudad_de_Mexico" title="Ciudad de Mexico">Ciudad de Mexico</a>, daughter of Aztec princess <a href="/wiki/Isabel_Moctezuma" title="Isabel Moctezuma">Tecuichpotzin</a> (baptized Isabel), born in Tenochtitlan on July 11, 1510 and died on July 9, 1550, the eldest legitimate daughter of Moctezuma II Xocoyotzin and wife <i>doña</i> María Miahuaxuchitl; married to <a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Tolosa" title="Juan de Tolosa">Juan de Tolosa</a>, a Basque merchant and miner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>doña</i> María Cortés de Moctezuma, daughter of an Aztec princess; nothing more is known about her except that she probably was born with some deformity.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
<p>He married twice: firstly in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a> to Catalina Suárez Marcaida, who died at <a href="/wiki/Coyoac%C3%A1n" title="Coyoacán">Coyoacán</a> in 1522 without issue, and secondly in 1529 to <i>doña</i> Juana Ramírez de Arellano de Zúñiga, daughter of <i>don</i> Carlos Ramírez de Arellano, 2nd Count of Aguilar and wife the Countess <i>doña</i> Juana de Zúñiga, and had:</p>
<ul>
<li><i>don</i> Luis Cortés y Ramírez de Arellano, born in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texcoco,_Mexico" title="Texcoco, Mexico">Texcoco</a> in 1530 and died shortly after his birth.</li>
<li><i>doña</i> Catalina Cortés de Zúñiga, born in <a href="/wiki/Cuernavaca" title="Cuernavaca">Cuernavaca</a> in 1531 and died shortly after her birth.</li>
<li><i>don</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mart%C3%ADn_Cort%C3%A9s,_2nd_Marqu%C3%A9s_del_Valle_de_Oaxaca" title="Martín Cortés, 2nd Marqués del Valle de Oaxaca">Martín Cortés</a> y Ramírez de Arellano, 2nd Marquis of the Valley of Oaxaca, born in <a href="/wiki/Cuernavaca" title="Cuernavaca">Cuernavaca</a> in 1532, married at <a href="/wiki/Nalda" title="Nalda">Nalda</a> on February 24, 1548 his twice cousin once removed <i>doña</i> Ana Ramírez de Arellano y Ramírez de Arellano and had issue, currently extinct in male line</li>
<li><i>doña</i> María Cortés de Zúñiga, born in <a href="/wiki/Cuernavaca" title="Cuernavaca">Cuernavaca</a> between 1533 and 1536, married to <i>don</i> Luis de Quiñones y Pimentel, 5th Count of Luna</li>
<li><i>doña</i> Catalina Cortés de Zúñiga, born in <a href="/wiki/Cuernavaca" title="Cuernavaca">Cuernavaca</a> between 1533 and 1536, died unmarried in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sevilla" title="Sevilla">Sevilla</a> after the funeral of her father</li>
<li><i>doña</i> Juana Cortés de Zúñiga, born in <a href="/wiki/Cuernavaca" title="Cuernavaca">Cuernavaca</a> between 1533 and 1536, married Don Fernando Enríquez de Ribera y Portocarrero, 2nd Duke of <a href="/wiki/Alcal%C3%A1_de_los_Gazules" title="Alcalá de los Gazules">Alcalá de los Gazules</a>, 3rd Marquess of <a href="/wiki/Tarifa" title="Tarifa">Tarifa</a> and 6th Count of <a href="/wiki/Los_Molares" title="Los Molares">Los Molares</a>, and had issue</li>
</ul>
